It's a great feature for enterprises, but it requires careful engineering. (The thickness and material of the walls in older dorms doesn't help!) \n\nPart of the problem is that home wireless routers come out of the box amped up to provide you with coverage throughout your home without much regard for other signals. It's similar to playing a different radio station at a really high volume; it will still interfere with one's ability to \"hear\" other channels. \n\nThis is really the issue at hand. Josh is right to point out that bandwidth is not really affected; the throughput of a network isn't affected because someone connects via wireless rather than wired. The degradation of TAMULink signal (and the associated degradation of performance) is the issue.\n\nAlso, at the end of the day, TAMU is required by Texas law to control the means of access to the campus network. Allowing unmonitored wireless connections in the dorms (meaning, TAMU can't ensure it has a password, or to whom you might give that password) violates this mandate.\n\n(Full disclosure: I'm part of the support team for TAMU IT.
